‘sect TYPIC/AMBUD/Operational
s_AMTRIGON-8 (201-283995), AMBUD Case #97

‘ASTON ACQUIRED: MCRD
Reference: UFGW-7040, 29 April 1968
1, AMTRIGON-8 was a member of the VILLARO crew. During
May 1962 he clandestinely and without authcrization boarded an
infiltration craft moments before its departure on an

operational mission, His absence was not discovered until the
team had infiltrated and moved into its first position,

2, On 8 or 9 June 1962 the infiltration team, . including
AMTRIGON-8, became engaged in a firefight with a militia
patrol, AMTRIGON~-2, the tdam leader, reported that AMTRIGON-8
had been wounded and that he assumed AMTRIGON-8 was killed
or perhaps captured. However, no further word has been heard
from AMTRIGON-8 and he is presumed to be dead,

3, ‘Taking into consideration that the disposition of this
case could have an affect on the morale of the other crew
members and their attitude toward WOFIRM, it was decided to
advise the widow of AMTRIGON-8 that he died a hero's death-
while fighting for the liberation.of his country and to continue
monthly payments to the widow-and:children for an indefinite
period. Inclusion of Subject‘’s name on AMBUD Hero & Martyr
rolls was deémed to be.'the most suitable ‘aad expeditious manner

in which to handle si ich payments,

4, The response to paragraph 2 of reférence will be
the subject of a separate dispatch.

BUD _Depondoncy Cases

1, It is requested that Kaymond K, PANUSES recheck the file
of Miguel Los Santos DELGADO Martinez (Case No. 97) An an effort
to determine the cause and actual date of his death. Headquarters
file does not reflect this information nor the rexson why his
dependents are paid under. the AMBUD program. In those few cuses
of former active assets whose-dependents are paid by AMTIKI, the
exact, date and circumstance of death is necessary fur documentation,

2, It is nlso requested that ANTIKI be queried regarding
certain vital documents which should be in the file of Benito
BLANCO Cruz (Case No. 3), A copy of a letter from the widow.
dated 11 Junuary 1962, indicated that her marriage certificate
and the birth cortificates of her children were enclosed with the
letter, It is poss{tble, but unlikely, these documents were over-
looked‘when the file was recently reviewed, In any event, the
work check sheet used by the documentation team indicntes these

documents were missing from the file,

1. Headquorters recommends that 211 reference accounts, with
the possible exception of the PASTKANA account (Case #118), be
closed immediately and the proceeds transferred to Headquarters,

2. It 1s suggested that AMTIKI be queried concerning any
possible embarrassment: he might suffer in his personal relation-
ship with the bank {fhe_summarily cloges all the accounts, since
there is no wish to place him in an untenable position. Head~
quarters is avare that these so-called trust accounts aro actually
savings accounts and wore so designated on the 1967 bank statemonts
filed in the AMTIKI files, Under the circumstances, it is highly
possible thst an IRS inquiry may be initiated after the accounts
are withdrawn and AMTIKI should be assured of Headquarters inter-
cession in his behalf if ho is questioned by IRS. However, in
the event of such an inquiry, lloadquarters must be proparod to
submit a full accounting of these casow including dates and amounts
of deposits and withdrawals ond WOFIRM authorization for trans-
actions which JH¥AVE should bé able to provide, It 18 recommended
that AUTIKI immediately prepare a full background history relating
to the opening of each account, #11 financial transactions since
the accounts were opened, and referencos to JMWAVE authorization
for any deposits and withdrawals, These accountings should be

. forwarded for Headquarters filos 98 soon as they are comploted.
When AMTIKI is suthorized to close the accounts, a memorandum
covering the authorization should be prepared by, JMWAVE ond a

copy forwarded to Headquarters.
3. In the event above recommendations tend to create any _

insursountable probloms JMWAVE, is requested to advise the nature
of the problems and submit alternate recommendations,

Ellen F. MARGANY

1. ‘The monthly payment made to the dependents of
Ovidio CANEJU Lopez was reduced by $25,00 effective
1 April 1968 inasmuch 29 Station and AMTIXI-1 fi}
indicated that Subjoct's son, Miguel Angel CAMEJO-Rojas,
had reached 21 yoars of age on 11 March 1968,

_ 2. Upon being informed of the payment reduction,
Subject's widow, Blanca ROJAS, advised AUTIKI-1 by letter
that the correct birth date of her son is 11 March 1948
and not 11 March 1947., Subsequently, the widow provided
a photostatic copy of her son's INS-issued residence card
(copy attached) which records bie birth date as 11 March

1948.

3, Accordingly, AMTII-1 has been instructed to
reinstate the $25.00 sum retroactive to 1 April 1968,

REFERENCES; UFGA-29508

JMWAVE-1613
DIR 83308

1. AMTIKI-1 has contacted the bank regarding the Social
Security numbers requested and has been advised that, although
the bank is not obligated to insist upon Social Security or other
identifying numbers for. these accounts, it does feel that ANTIKI-1
may ultimately be subjected to an inquiry from the Internal Revenue
Service. Their reasoning is based primarily upon the fact that
the accounts, while trust accounts for our purposes, are not true
trust accounts in that no trust agreements are of record at the
bank. (Trust agreements could not be signed, of course, since the
individuals were not and are not available to sign.)

2. In order to protect AMTIKI-1 from any possible IRS
investigation and, rat he matter further with the
bank, for which we hav it is suggested that
these accounts be closed out over a two or three month period and
re-established at Headquarters through the appropriate DTEARN
channels, If the accounts remain here, it will be necessary to
prepare new signature cards for each account removing Humphrey 0,
TIMANUS as a signatory and adding a JMCOBRA asset as ‘an "inside"
trustee for control purposes, or to remove ANTIKI-1 entirely and
establish the JMCOBSRA asset as the sole trustee.

3. Please : advise,

1. .AMTIKI-1 roceived a letter dated 19 Septembor 1967 fron
a lawyer representing Higuelena Teurbe FRITZ requesting information
ag to why “payments to tho specifically named bencficiaries in your
policy if you have ono, or those who would normally recoive the
proceeds of a death benefit if you do not bave a policy" had been

terminated.
2. A review of thie caso reveals the following:

~,@.  Miguolona’.Teurbe FRITZ was advised by a letter dated

7 31 December 1966 that it had been ascertained that she waa not
entitled to monthly payments as the widow of Roberto PEREZ Cruzata
since sho ‘had neyor married PEREZ. Tho letter 'alao advised. that
payments heretofore sent to Mrs: FRITZ for her daughter and the
parents of PEREZ were likewiso being terminated because it had been
learned tbat her daughter, Kathleen FRITZ, is not related to PEREZ
in any manner, thatthe mother had died, ‘and that there is not
evidence that the father in Cuba had received any of the funds

intended for hin.
: b. Shortly thereafter, urs. FRITZ requested that the

matter be reconsidered sinco she had not been givon ‘advance notice
of the termination and because the abrupt halt in payments created

& severe economic hardship for her.
c. She was then advised by letter that the payment

enclosed with the termination notice was for January 1967 and was
intended to provide a one-month notice of the payment termination,

{8880 TYPIC/ANDUD /Operat ional
equest from Widow of Angel PASTRANA Santos (Case #118) for Assistance

ActiOw RLQURLO-RUNLEINUS in’ Leaving Cuba.
ACTION REQUIRED: Soo para 3

References: A. UFGH=-6607, 13 July 1967
B. UFGA-27805, 14 June 1967

1... As suggested in Reference. B, ANTIKI~1 adviged the widow
that the only legal means for purchasing passage from Cuba. to
Spain with US dollars was by purchasing the passage at Iberia.
Airlines® Madrid office, In a letter dated 11 Soptembor 1967,
the widow acknowledged receipt of the lotter from AMTIKI~1 and
Stated that sho bad contacted the Iberia office in Havana and had
-been;told that this proceduro -is no longe-\ allowed. The widow
then went to the National Bank of Cuba where she was advised that

the only way ehe.could purchase: passage would be to recoivo funds
in Canadian currency through tl Cuban bank. _ The bank suggested
that the fastest ‘way to effect the transaction would be to have
the money sent by telegraphic transfer through a Canadian bank

to tho National Bank of Cuba.

2. A check with the Iberia Airlines representative in the
JHWAVE area confirmed that: the procedure suggested by Headquarters’
is not permissible. The representative stated that the procedure

suggested by the National Bank .of Cuba was correct, adding that
‘a Spanish bank and Spanish currency could. be utilized instead of

Canadian if so desired. :

3. Headquarters guidance regarding the adviseability of*
effecting such a transfer of: funds to Cuba through Canada or Spain
Attached are copies of recent correspondence con-

is requested.
- cerning this case,

Havana, 17 August 1967

COCONUT GROVE. BANK ; :
MIAMI, FLORIDA Ef 7 : Attention: Mr, Administrator

4

Sir:

Iam writing to you to ask you to do me the favor of informing

“\< Mg, Join Paulbath that I urgently necd’Win to contact me because

I’want him to send the-passages to me to go (to the U,S,) via Spain.

The reason I have taken the liberty of writing is that in
November of last year, I wrote to Mr, Paulbath ot PO Box 427, Tamiami
Station in that city and after almost six months the letter was
“returned tome with the notation that the address was not registered.
Since that time a friend of mine who lives in Los Angeles has been
trying to locate him and to date has had no success,

Mr; Paulbath sent-me.a notice informing that the monthly stipend
due me (os a result of ‘the death of my husband) per dotal policy 1023,_
was béing depésited in that bank, enclosed is that notice, . The
last news I Nad from Mr, Paulbath was. in February 1966 when-he informed
me that on that date the account showed a balance of US $12,518.21.

i appeal to your kindness for help, since I have been ‘trying

for more than six years since my husband died R.I,P, to leave (Cuba).
I aktsmua almost. had a11 my. papers. in order to leave when the. American
Embassy was closed that was two months after my husband ‘had -departed
(Cuba), later in April of ‘that same year came the Bay of Pigs Invasion
and my husband’was killed, On 1 June my daughter vas, born yand it was,
‘at this time that. they began to grant ‘visa woiversxbut even though” t'*
had the visas I ‘could not lefive because I had not Deen able. to get
a passport for my daughter since to obtain it they demanded my husband's
death ‘certificate and his death was not recorded in any court, I went

. to.all the places it could have been recorded, Then I began to visit
lawyers and ‘government offices’ to find out how I could obtain a passport
for my daughter, After much fighting, it was delivered to me.at the
end of November of last year. I immediately wrote to Mr. Paulbath
to ask that he send me the money ‘for passages right away, and that was
the letter that was returned to me,

Since letters from there to here take so long, I request that
you tell Mr, Poulbath to send me the money for passages for: those

indicated below:
Concepcion PASTRANA Cernuda (US $154,00)

Serafin CERNUDA Garcia (US $308.00) ; :
Graciela CERNUDA Fernandez. (US $308.00) - ?
Maria CERNUDA Fernandez (US $308.00)

and also tell him that the money for all should be sent to the

following address:
Colina #33, Jesus del Monte, Habana, Cuba,


mete

RANA STR tsa

Tell Mr, Paulbath that if there is snything 1 can resolve -call
me at telephone number 99+2187 or sond mea night letter since xeguak
regular mail takes up to one and one half months to arrive.

Attentively, *

21 September 1967

Habana, Cuba

Dear Mrs, Cernuda:

I received your letter of 17 August today and in accordance
with your wishes, I talked with Mr, John Paulbath to explain what
you need, In addition, I am sending him a copy of your lettor
dated 17 August. .

Mr. Paulbath promised me that he would immediately look into
this matter and when you desire to communicote with him you may
write to me if you would like. I hope that your problem will
be resolved promptly.

Attentively,

A.P, Betancourt
Senior Vice President —

a Dear Mr.
As per your request, I tried to obtain copy of my marriage
certificate from Cuba, Despite my efforts I havo been
unable to secure one.

However, copics of my husband's and my daughter's birth
certificates, issued some time ago, were forwarded to
me.

Marginal note on my husband's certificate shows entry of
our marriage and our daughter's also mentions the fact of

said marriage.

I am enclosing photocopies of both documents, Should you
require the originals, I will be happy to forward them. to
you as long as they are returned to me since these are the
only copics in my possessioh.

I will continue to try to secure copy of my marriage cer~
tificate which I will forward to you, should I obtain it.

Trusting these documents will be of heip to you, I am,

Very truly yours

Marina Mardones Vivanco

i 1, Headquarters concurs in JEWAVE's proposed action
refusing payment of additional funds to Subject of reference.
Apparently Subject had not advised AMBIDDY of the regular
Support pnyments paid by AMTIKI at the timo reference B ro-
quested data concerning the case. Neither is there any
indication on the HEY form forwardod in reference C that
additional income was being recoived by Subject from AMBIDDY.
_It_would, therefore, appear that AMBIDDY mony have indicated — _
there was some connection botween the source of AHNTIKI and
AMBIDDY funds and suggested Subject approach AMTIKI for the
terminated AMBIDDY income.

' 2. In.any event, subject letter did provide copies of
the type of vital documents JNWAVE is attempting to obtain in
order to document Heroes and Martyra for possible future
payments by BEC.

TRANSLATI:

Dear Mr. Lo}

In your letter of 1 May 1967 you asked me for my marriage.
certificate and my son's birth certificate, I do not havo them
because my home was immediately intervened by the so-called
Comandante Felix Torres who burned my family passport and wouldn't
My cousin (?), Porfirjo’s —

even let me get my son's clothing,

brother Rodolfo RAMIREZ same clandestinely went to the coasts of

Cuba to get me. I am sending you photostatic copies of our
I believe they will suffice but at the samo time

Parolee cards.

I will write to Porfirio's mother who is still in Cuba since
she has not been given permission to leave and come to this country

and I will ask her to “get copics of the marriage certificate,

Chicago, May 8, 1967

I will send them to you as soon as I receive then,

Thanks again,
/s/ Clara DELGADO

AETON REQUIRED ROTTRENCED

° FERNANDEZ further stated that there are actually two bank accounts

‘docurentation froa

Reference: UFGH-6306, 8 December 1966

: : r

1. The information requested by Headquarters in paragraph two

of Reference concerning tho funds held in trust for Jorgo GUTIERREZ

Izaguirro (prisoner) has been obtained from the trustee, Mr. Orlando
FERKANDEZ and is forwarded herewith.

&
2. According to Mr. FERHANDEZ, an arrangement wi'th the family
of Subject provides that Hr. FERNANDEZ (who now resides in Tampa)
receive the monthly payment of $225.00 and forward it to an uncle of
Subject, Lvelio CORZO (in Miami), who is responsible for the forward-
ing of aseistance to the Bubject and bis parents in Cuba. Mr.

which he described as follows:

a. Dade Federal Savings and Loan Association,
Miawi, Plorida, account number 04-439677. January 1967
balance: $6,748.36. The account is in the name of Bubject's
uncle and aunt, Evolio and Lillian CORZO.

b. The Exchange Lank of Temple Terrace, Taspa, Florida,
account number 3627. January 1967 balance: $675.00. The
account is in the name of the trustee, Mr. Orlando FEHNANDEZ,

M.. FERNANDEZ explained the reason for two bank accounts as
follows: During the time that the trustee resided in Miami, the check
was deposited by Mr. CORZO in the CORZO account. When the trustee
moved to Tampa (date unknown) Mr. CORZO told the trustee that in view
of the ample funds on deposit ir Miawi, the trustee should open a
Savings account in Tampa for the deposit of future payments.

CUBAN DEMOCRATIC REVCLUTIONARY FRONT
FINANCE DEPARTMENT

RESUME OF_THE INCOME AND EXPENSES OPERATIONS
"PAULA _AND_SOSA"

October _1 to 31, 1960

In the financial statements and annex the analysis and sub-analysis of
each one of the income and liabilities during the month of October are
shown,
Receipts, invoices, deposit slips and other papers are kept in our files.
As shown on Annex "I-D", a Revolving Fund has been created for the Mili-
tary Section, amounting.to the sume of $10,000.00, divided into two parts
of $5,000.00 each, the amount- of $3,387.81, was reinbursed to this Revoly
ing Fund, as per Annex "I-D",

The amount of %50,000,00 which appears as "Transferences® in Annex "I-M*
corresponds to the transfered amount from the account of "Paula and Sosa”
to "Rasco and Paula” account.

From this amount, we have paid in advance the November payment of the.
military dependants.

In relation to "Checks to Justify", amounting to $69,288.52, as per =
Annex "I-P", these could be classified in two groups; one formed by -
those corresponding to amounts advanced accouding to budget to the -
different Committees and Delegations and the other, formed by certain
expenses to be made, but specifically determined, with receipts dully
signed. The later could have. been distributed to those accounts with-

in the cassification, thus eliminating them from the title "to justify",
but have been kept as so, to be sure of the making of this expense for
the purpose to which the checks were drown for, or its actual classific-
ation, if these expense were made for other purposes than those original-
ly aimed to, This is due to the fact that some checks were drawn for a
specific purpose; they could also have been applied te acquire some =
other asset, thus appearing at the end of the month a filse balance, since
it would appear as an expense, what it actually is an asset.

Section designated as "Transferences" $50,000.00 is Compensated with an
anconwe for tne same amount, when making a transference of runds’ to the
"Rasco and Paula” account to pay through it the payroll of the Military
